“你刚才说Slide7和Slide12的Wegovy FY2025数字(DKK79.1B/USD12.0B)一致，但你检索到的Novo Nordisk 2025年报原文里写的是‘Wegovy销售额增长到DKK51,015 million’——这两个数字(79.1B vs 51.0B)差了将近28B，到底哪个对？这是不是说明你的核心数字之一根本经不起核查？”

✓ 标准回答 / ANSWER
中文：这是一个非常好的核查点，我需要诚实地说：目前能确认的是‘79.1B/12B’这个数字在Slide7和Slide12两页之间是‘内部一致’的(同一个数字被两页共同引用，没有相互矛盾)，但我还没有把它和年报‘按产品线披露的收入注释(revenue by product note)’逐项核对到‘精确匹配某一行’的程度。‘DKK51,015 million’这句话出现在年报正文的业务进展叙述部分，但财报里同一个产品的销售额，有时会在‘业务回顾(business review)’和‘财务报表附注(notes to financial statements)’两处出现不同的统计区间(例如一处是‘本季度’，另一处是‘全年累计’，或一处含税/不含税、一处是‘net sales’vs‘gross sales’)——这两个数字之间28B的差距，大概率来自统计区间或口径差异，而不是‘其中一个是编造的’。在正式提交前，我会做的核查步骤是：打开年报‘Notes to the financial statements’里‘Segment information’或‘Revenue by product’表，找到Wegovy 2025全年(Jan-Dec)的单一行数字，用那个数字替换或确认‘79.1B’，并在脚注里标注‘精确财报附注页码’。如果最终核实后数字有调整，我会同步修改Slide7和Slide12两处，保持一致。我想强调的是：这种‘同一数字、不同口径’的差异，在大型跨国公司财报里很常见，核查的关键不是‘哪个数字看起来更大/更小’，而是‘找到该数字在年报里最权威、统计区间最明确的那一处’。

EN: This is an excellent check, and the honest answer is: I can confirm "79.1B/12B" is internally consistent between Slides 7 and 12 (the same figure is used on both, with no contradiction between them), but I have not yet reconciled it line-by-line against the Annual Report's revenue-by-product note. "DKK51,015 million" appears in the narrative business-review section of the report, but the same product's sales figure can appear under different bases in different sections — e.g., a single quarter vs. full-year cumulative, or gross vs. net sales — and a ~28B gap is far more likely to reflect a basis/period difference than one figure being fabricated. Before finalizing, my next step would be to open the "Segment information" or "Revenue by product" note in the financial statements, locate the single full-year (Jan–Dec 2025) Wegovy figure, and either confirm or correct "79.1B" against it, citing the exact note/page, and propagate any correction to both Slide 7 and Slide 12 to preserve consistency. The key point: this kind of same-number-different-basis discrepancy is common in large multinational financial reports, and the resolution is to find the most authoritative, period-explicit instance of the figure — not to assume either number is simply wrong.

4. 面试官深度追问 / Deep-Dive Grilling — 财务数据和比较逻辑被质疑

更完整的六家企业逐一档案见"案例框架与公司深度资料 → 6. 公司深度档案"。这里是这一页最容易被追问的两个具体点。

[HIGH] 你展示恒瑞约86%毛利率——但这是全公司的，不是GLP-1专项。这不会产生误导吗？

⚠ ATTACK "You show Hengrui at ~86% gross margin — but that's company-wide, not GLP-1 specific. Isn't this misleading?"

EN： The slide explicitly states "company-level gross margin, not product-level" — disclosed in the source footnote, column header says "Overall Gross Margin." I use it to characterize the financial quality of the business as a whole — a company with 86% gross margin has strong unit economics that could support aggressive marketing investment when its GLP-1 product launches. I cannot show product-level GLP-1 obesity margin because no company discloses it separately. Using overall gross margin as a proxy for business quality is standard in equity research for early-stage pipeline companies where product-level economics aren't yet observable.

中：幻灯片明确标注"公司整体毛利率，非产品级别"——来源脚注和列标题均标明"Overall Gross Margin"。我用它描述整体业务的财务质量——86%整体毛利率的公司具有强劲的单位经济性，可在GLP-1产品上市时支撑积极的营销投入。无法展示GLP-1肥胖专项毛利率，因为没有公司单独披露。对于产品级经济性尚不可观测的早期管线公司，用整体毛利率作为业务质量代理在股权研究中是标准做法。

[MEDIUM] 你提到信达信尔美的"礼来中国境外授权"——但礼来已经是竞争对手了？

⚠ ATTACK "You include Innovent's Mazdutide with 'Eli Lilly ex-China licensing' — but isn't Eli Lilly already a competitor with Mufengda?"

EN： Valid observation. Eli Lilly plays two roles simultaneously: ① a direct competitor in China via its own product Mufengda (tirzepatide); ② a commercialization partner for Innovent's mazdutide outside China, where Lilly holds rights. This dual role isn't unusual in pharma — companies often partner on a mechanism outside their core geography while competing within it. The ex-China Lilly licensing validates mazdutide's clinical profile from a sophisticated counterparty's view — Lilly accepted the risk after seeing the data. Within China, the two companies are direct competitors. I note this complexity rather than oversimplifying it.

中：合理观察。礼来在这个市场同时扮演两个角色：①在中国直接竞争，通过自有产品穆峰达（替尔泊肽）；②作为信达信尔美在中国境外的商业化合作伙伴。这种双重角色在医药行业并不罕见——公司经常在自己的核心地区外对某机制做合作，同时在该地区内直接竞争。礼来境外授权从复杂对手视角验证了信尔美的临床价值——礼来在看到数据后接受了风险。在中国境内，两家公司是直接竞争关系。我在幻灯片上标注了这种复杂性而非过度简化。

Slide 13 Trends & Takeaways 趋势与结论

Five Structural Trends & Key Takeaways — Detailed Line-by-Line Analysis (Bilingual)
Overview

本文档逐元素拆解第13页：每句话的目的、数据来源、逻辑、可能被攻击的点和标准回答。 *This document breaks down Slide 13 element by element: purpose, data source, logic, attack points, and standard answers.*

1. 标题与副标题 Title & Subtitle

中文

原文：标题“FIVE STRUCTURAL TRENDS & KEY TAKEAWAYS”；副标题“China GLP-1 Obesity: Large Demand, Early Market, Access Is the Bottleneck”；页码“12”(对应第13张slide，延续封面不计页码的惯例)。

这一页在全篇里的位置——“收口页”：Slide10算出了2025年市场有多大(264/416/612M)，Slide11展示了2025-2030的演变路径和5个驱动因素(Price/Access/Product Unlocks)，Slide12比较了5家公司的财务定位。Slide13是整份报告的最后一页(从文本看“12”是最后一个页码)，它的任务不是引入新数据，而是把前面所有页的内容收拢成一句话结论。标题里的“KEY TAKEAWAYS”直接点明了这一页的功能——“takeaway”是给读者/面试官‘带走的东西’，不是新的分析素材。

“FIVE STRUCTURAL TRENDS”与Slide11“5张driver卡片”的关系：这是一个非常重要的结构对照——这一页的5张卡片(01-05)和Slide11右侧的5张driver卡片，标题词高度重合(Biosimilar Price / Domestic Innovation / NRDL / Oral & Multi-Agonists / Access Ecosystem)，但标签(NEAR-TERM/CONFIRMED/SCENARIO/EMERGING/STRUCTURAL)的顺序和Slide11不完全一致。Slide11是“按照Growth Trigger Timeline的时间顺序排列”(2025→2030)，强调“什么时候会发生”；Slide13是“按照标题‘FIVE STRUCTURAL TRENDS’重新归类后呈现”，强调“这5件事分别是什么性质”。也就是说，同一组5个驱动因素，在Slide11里被组织成‘时间线’，在Slide13里被组织成‘结论清单’——这是“同一份素材、两种叙事顺序”的设计，体现了报告从‘过程’(process，Slide11)到‘结论’(conclusion，Slide13)的收尾。

副标题的三段式结构——“Large Demand, Early Market, Access Is the Bottleneck”：这句话本身就是整份报告的“一句话摘要”，三个短语精确对应三组数据：①“Large Demand”对应Slide1的587M超重肥胖人口(疾病负担)；②“Early Market”对应Slide10的渗透率<1.2%、2025年USD416M(Base Case)的市场规模——“早期”是相对587M的潜在人群而言；③“Access Is the Bottleneck”是这一页的核心论点，直接呼应Slide11副标题里的“Access”(NRDL+NHC政策)以及本页卡片05“Access Ecosystem Build”。三个短语用逗号连接、层层递进，构成了一个“因为A(需求大)+B(市场早期)，所以C(瓶颈在可及性，不在需求或技术)”的论证链条——这是整份报告‘从591M到416M’这条主线索的终极浓缩版。

为什么副标题不说“Access Is THE Bottleneck”里用定冠词“THE”而不是“A”：用“THE”而不是“A”，是把“access”定位为唯一的、最关键的瓶颈，排除了“需求不足”或“技术/疗效不够”作为主要瓶颈的可能性——这是一个很强的论断，需要前面所有页的数据来支撑(587M需求、6款已获批产品、SELECT/SURMOUNT等疗效证据)。这个措辞选择本身就是一个需要在答辩时能够“拆解支撑”的论点，而不只是一句修辞。

EN

Original text: Title "FIVE STRUCTURAL TRENDS & KEY TAKEAWAYS"; subtitle "China GLP-1 Obesity: Large Demand, Early Market, Access Is the Bottleneck"; page number "12" (the final page number in the deck, following the cover-page-not-numbered convention).

This page's role — the closing page: Slide 10 sized the 2025 market (264/416/612M), Slide 11 mapped the 2025–2030 trajectory and five drivers (Price/Access/Product Unlocks), Slide 12 compared five companies' financial positioning. Slide 13 is the deck's final page; its job isn't to introduce new data but to compress everything into one takeaway. "KEY TAKEAWAYS" signals exactly this — something for the audience to walk away with, not new analytical material.

"FIVE STRUCTURAL TRENDS" vs. Slide 11's five driver cards: An important structural parallel — the five cards here (01–05) share nearly identical headline labels with Slide 11's driver cards (Biosimilar Price / Domestic Innovation / NRDL / Oral & Multi-Agonists / Access Ecosystem), but the confidence tags (NEAR-TERM/CONFIRMED/SCENARIO/EMERGING/STRUCTURAL) are NOT in the same order as Slide 11. Slide 11 orders them along the Growth Trigger Timeline (2025→2030), emphasizing WHEN; Slide 13 re-groups them around the title's "structural trends" framing, emphasizing WHAT KIND. The same five drivers are organized as a timeline on Slide 11 and as a conclusions list on Slide 13 — the same material narrated twice, once as process and once as conclusion.

The subtitle's three-part structure — "Large Demand, Early Market, Access Is the Bottleneck": This sentence is the report's one-line abstract. Each phrase maps to a data set: ① "Large Demand" → Slide 1's 587M overweight/obese adults (disease burden); ② "Early Market" → Slide 10's sub-1.2% penetration and ~USD416M (Base Case) 2025 market — "early" relative to the 587M potential pool; ③ "Access Is the Bottleneck" is this page's core thesis, echoing Slide 11's "Access" (NRDL + NHC policy) and this page's Card 05 ("Access Ecosystem Build"). Connected by commas in a build-up, the structure is "because A (huge demand) + B (early-stage market), therefore C (the bottleneck is access, not demand or technology)" — the ultimate condensation of the report's '587M → 416M' throughline.

Why "THE" bottleneck, not "A" bottleneck: Using the definite article positions access as the single, primary bottleneck, ruling out insufficient demand or insufficient efficacy as the main constraint — a strong claim that needs to be backed by everything established earlier (587M demand, 6 approved products, SELECT/SURMOUNT efficacy evidence). This word choice is itself a claim that should be defensible point-by-point in a defense session, not just rhetorical framing.

⚠ 攻击点 / ATTACK
“你说‘Access Is THE Bottleneck’，排除了‘需求不足’和‘疗效不够’这两个可能性——但Slide1的587M本身就是‘理论疾病负担’，不代表587M人都‘有意愿/有能力’去治疗。如果连‘需求’本身都没有被验证(只是‘患病’不等于‘想治疗’)，你怎么能说‘瓶颈不在需求’？”

✓ 标准回答 / ANSWER
中文：这个问题问得很准，它其实点出了‘demand’这个词在两个不同层面上的含义——‘疾病层面的需求(disease-level demand，587M)’和‘治疗意愿层面的需求(treatment-seeking demand)’。Slide9的funnel分析(从587M到181K的逐层收窄)里，恰恰把‘treatment-seeking willingness’作为一个独立的筛选层级单独列出，而不是假设‘有病=想治’。所以‘Large Demand’这个词，在副标题里指的是第一层(疾病负担层)——这是有NHC/Lancet数据支撑、几乎没有争议的事实；而‘Access Is the Bottleneck’这句话，是在承认治疗意愿本身可能也不是100%的前提下，指出‘在已经表达了治疗意愿、并且被诊断、符合适应症的那一部分人里，能不能真正用上药，才是当前最大的限制因素’。换句话说，这句话的完整逻辑链是：‘587M人里，一部分有诊断、有意愿(这部分本身已经被Slide9的diagnosis%和eligibility%筛选过)；在这部分人里，‘能不能buy到/报不报销/有没有渠道’(access)，比‘药效好不好/有没有合适的药’(technology，已经有6款获批+SELECT/SURMOUNT证据)更稀缺’——瓶颈是相对的、是在‘已经筛过一轮的人群’里做的判断，不是说‘587M人全都想治、全都被技术满足、只差access’这种绝对化的表述。如果汇报时被这样追问，可以直接说：‘您说得对，587M本身不是‘想治疗的人数’，这正是Slide9 funnel要做的事——这句话的‘demand’说的是‘疾病层面的需求规模’，‘bottleneck’说的是‘在已经被筛选过一层(diagnosis+eligibility)的人群里，下一步卡在哪里’。’

EN: This question correctly identifies that "demand" operates at two different levels — disease-level demand (587M) versus treatment-seeking demand. Slide 9's funnel (587M down to ~181K) explicitly treats treatment-seeking willingness as its own filtering layer, rather than assuming disease = desire to treat. So "Large Demand" in the subtitle refers to the disease-burden layer — well-supported by NHC/Lancet data and largely uncontroversial. "Access Is the Bottleneck" is then made conditional on having already passed through diagnosis and eligibility filtering: among people who ARE diagnosed and eligible, what limits them most is whether they can actually obtain the drug (afford it, get it reimbursed, access a channel) rather than whether an effective drug exists (6 approved products, SELECT/SURMOUNT evidence already establish efficacy). The bottleneck claim is thus relative — made about an already-filtered population — not an absolute claim that all 587M want treatment and are only blocked by access. A good response: "You're right that 587M isn't the number of people seeking treatment — that's exactly what Slide 9's funnel addresses. 'Demand' here refers to disease-level scale; 'bottleneck' refers to what blocks the next step, for the population that has already cleared diagnosis and eligibility."
